\section*{Phase 4 --- Proof Log (running record)}

This folder is the \textbf{permanent working record} of the pure-math proof attempt. Every derivation,\par
dead end, and partial result is logged here so nothing is lost. Each working file is self-contained\par
and dated; this log is the index + chronology.\par

\textbf{Conventions.} Hilbert space, operator, and notation are *pinned once* in\par
\texttt{A1-operator-and-compression.md} ?1 and reused everywhere. When a\par
file proves something, it is promoted to a numbered \textbf{Result} (Lemma/Prop/Thm) and copied into the\par
ledger below. Honest status tags: [OK] proved \ensuremath{\cdot} ? reduced-to / conditional \ensuremath{\cdot} ? open \ensuremath{\cdot} [X] refuted.\par

\medskip\hrule\medskip

\subsection*{Files}
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{A1-operator-and-compression.md} --- \textbf{Problem A.} Pins
\end{itemize}
  $(\mathcal H,\mathcal T)$; states and reduces the compression identity $Q=P_J\mathcal T P_J$.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{B2-semiboundedness.md} --- \textbf{Problem B-2.} Semiboundedness of the Weil
\end{itemize}
  form; the KLMN attack and where arithmetic cancellation becomes unavoidable.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{B2.4a-de-branges-norm.md} --- \textbf{B2.4a / D(i).} The de Branges norm;
\end{itemize}
  Gamma-factor geometry, the width-$\tfrac12$ triple coincidence, and the reduction **B-2 $\rightsquigarrow$\par
  de Branges chain** (downgraded from \texttt{\textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}equiv\}} on Day 3).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{B2.4a-closability.md} --- \textbf{the bridge.} Closability of $\mathfrak t$ in
\end{itemize}
  $H(E)$; the sign/value invariance principle; closability $\iff$ (C-bound); the weight prerequisite (?0).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{B2.4a-break-attempt.md} --- \textbf{the break (Day 4) + RETRACTION (Day 5).} BR.1
\end{itemize}
  [X] false (hard-cutoff artifact); Fock pivot withdrawn; $H(E_\gamma)$ back in play.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{EF-identity-audit.md} --- \textbf{audit (Day 6).} The explicit-formula identity
\end{itemize}
  $\mathfrak t=\sum_\rho h(\gamma_\rho)$: unconditional on the dense core; RHS \textbf{indefinite} (not\par
  positive); closure in $H(E_\gamma)$ \textbf{open}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{closure-in-HEgamma.md} --- \textbf{first positive result (Day 7).} $\mathfrak t_+$
\end{itemize}
  \textbf{closed} (Kato); RH $\Rightarrow$ $\mathfrak t$ closable; the whole residual = **one KLMN inequality\par
  (RFB)** = a zero-density comparison. *(CLOS.1 overclaim corrected Day 8.)*\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{CLOS1-audit-and-RFB.md} --- \textbf{Day 8.} Part A: CLOS.1 audited --- "closure$=\mathfrak t_+$"
\end{itemize}
  \textbf{retracted}; form-core open. Part B: (RFB) is a \textbf{Carleson} condition; sufficient cond.\par
  $\sum K(t-ib,t-ib)<\infty$. *(Space corrected Day 9.)*\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{space-correction-strip-hardy.md} --- \textbf{Day 9 (deep dive).} Computing
\end{itemize}
  $K$ quantitatively suggests $H(E_\gamma)$ is \textbf{trace-class = TRIVIALIZES}; leading candidate the **strip\par
  Hardy space**. *(Trivialization downgraded to conditional Day 10.)*\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day10-kernel-audit.md} --- \textbf{Day 10 (audit of the load-bearing kernel).} Formula
\end{itemize}
  [OK]; trivialization \textbf{normalization-dependent} ($\blacklozenge$, Danger C real); gem: faithful $\Rightarrow S_{\mathrm{off}}=\infty$\par
  *(both F1 \& F2 found to have gaps Day 11)*.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day11-theorem-audit.md} --- \textbf{Day 11 (audit of the Day-10 theorem).} F2 false
\end{itemize}
  ($1/\log$); F1 conditional ($D(t)\ge0$ can fail); reconstructed \textbf{density-adapted} ($K\gtrsim1/\log$);\par
  impossibility-constraint list \textbf{K1--K4}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day12-density-scaling-law.md} --- \textbf{Day 12 (the scaling law).} Faithful
\end{itemize}
  $\iff K\rho\notin L^1$; \textbf{F1 = geometric (Level B)} via $D=2K_{11}-\tfrac12K''$; \textbf{necessary scaling law}\par
  $K\asymp1/\rho$; \textbf{A.2 = lower sampling bound} (upper=Carleson proved).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day13-DENS1-audit.md} --- \textbf{Day 13 (audit of DENS.1).} The fluctuation $\int K\,dS$
\end{itemize}
  is $O(\log\log T)\lll M$; DENS.1 \textbf{holds for regularly-varying $K$} (mild); critical law unconditional.\par
  First audited pillar to \textbf{hold up}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day14-reduction-audit.md} --- \textbf{Day 14 (audit of the A.2 reduction).} Genuine
\end{itemize}
  space = \textbf{over-sampling}; A.2 \ensuremath{\ne} frame bound; coercivity easy. *(Its T2/K5 mechanism corrected Day 15.)*\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day15-K5-audit.md} --- \textbf{Day 15 (audit of K5).} K5's "$R\asymp1\Rightarrow$ Carleson"
\end{itemize}
  is \textbf{false}: Carleson is governed by $P=\rho\ell$ ($\ell=\sqrt{K/K_{11}}$), not $R=K\rho$. Eval-bounding\par
  $\Rightarrow\ell\gtrsim\tfrac12\Rightarrow P\to\infty$ \textbf{always} \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} over-sampling FORCED; no T2.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day16-carleson-and-RFB.md} --- \textbf{Day 16 (Carleson + RFB proof).} $P\lesssim1\Rightarrow$
\end{itemize}
  Carleson (Schur, suff. only); $P\to\infty\Rightarrow\mathfrak t_+$ unbounded (direct kernel test). RFB sketch\par
  Step-3 hole; clean Schur-interpolation route \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} \textbf{RFB $\Leftarrow$ zero sampling-regularity} (the arithmetic).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day17-verification.md} --- \textbf{Day 17 (verification).} TWO errors in the deeper
\end{itemize}
  exploration: Montgomery-scale "reversal" (coherence\ensuremath{\ne}bandwidth; $P$ scale-invariant) and lattice/Schur\par
  (all $\ell^1$ routes hit $P\to\infty$). RFB plausibly TRUE $O(1)$ via $P$-\textbf{cancellation}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day18-quadrature.md} --- \textbf{Day 18 (quadrature reformulation).} RFB $\Leftarrow$
\end{itemize}
  \textbf{band-fixed quadrature} $\sum_\gamma|F(\gamma)|^2\approx\rho\int|F|^2$; $P$ cancels; reduces to the\par
  zeros' low-freq \textbf{form factor} (Montgomery). Most likely an \textbf{RH-conditional reformulation} ("new face").\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day19-pair-correlation-input.md} --- \textbf{Day 19 (the external input).}
\end{itemize}
  Parseval [OK] (cleaner in $PW_d$ = classical Weil class); $\|D_T\|^2_{L^2[-2d,2d]}$ = **scale-$1/d$ pair-corr\par
  2nd moment\textbf{ at }Montgomery's proven $\beta\to0$ range**. B-2 closes in $H_+$. Decisive: is $V(d,T)$\par
  unconditional?\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day20-threshold-correction.md} --- **Day 20 (the threshold push has a
\end{itemize}
  VACUOUS step).** Global $\sqrt{V(d,T)}$ Cauchy--Schwarz is vacuous ($\to\infty\cdot\mathfrak t_+$). Local\par
  IBP+Bernstein+Selberg \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $E_g=O(\mathfrak t_+)$ \textbf{unconditional}; $\kappa(b)\le e^d$. **B-2 plausibly\par
  unconditional** (no Montgomery).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day21-offline-and-coercivity.md} --- **Day 21 (off-line closed; B-2 \ensuremath{\Leftarrow}
\end{itemize}
  gaps).\textbf{ Proofs A/B/C verified. Off-line gap }closed unconditionally\textbf{ by }Plancherel--P\\\'olya** (clustering-OK)\par
  + local count $O(\rho)$ \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\widetilde{\mathfrak t}_-\le C_d\rho\|F\|_2^2$. \textbf{B-2 \textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}Leftarrow\} COERCIVITY}. *(Gap framing\par
  refined Day 22.)*\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{../PAPER-A.md} --- \textbf{Day 23 --- THE DELIVERABLE (paper A).} Full self-contained write-up:
\end{itemize}
  Theorem A (semibounded realization, modulo (H)), Theorem B (Kre?n $\mathfrak t=E^*JE$ + angular operator,\par
  $\|K\|\le1\iff$RH), Theorem C (no-go: zero-side can't reach the sign). All equations, prior-work placement\par
  (Connes--Consani, de Branges completion), honest scope. Author: David Alejandro Trejo Pizzo.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{../B2-THEOREM.md} --- \textbf{Day 23.} Complete B-2 theorem assembled: Lemmas A--D + depth
\end{itemize}
  split unconditional; hypothesis (H) isolated (\ensuremath{\ll} RH, frontier). RH \ensuremath{\iff} sign of finite bottom.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{../B3-KREIN-STRUCTURE.md} --- \textbf{Day 23.} Kre?n/angular structure verified +
\end{itemize}
  audited; ?8 \textbf{no-go theorem} (depth gives no leverage); over-claim "exactly Connes--Consani" corrected.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{../RH-ENDGAME.md} --- \textbf{Day 23.} Reconnection to RH: machinery gives FINITE bottom
\end{itemize}
  (B-2), RH = the SIGN; needs structural positivity $\mathcal T=A^*A$, untouched.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{Day22-coercivity.md} --- \textbf{Day 22 (coercivity = pure sampling).} $D^-=\infty$ does
\end{itemize}
  \textbf{NOT} give the lower frame bound (one Nyquist gap kills it --- referee right). \textbf{Depth split:} only \textbf{deep}\par
  off-line zeros ($\kappa$ large) are dangerous, and they're locally $o(\rho)$ by \textbf{short-interval zero-density};\par
  shallow ones harmless. \textbf{B-2 \textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}Leftarrow\} uniform short-interval zero-density} (\ensuremath{\ll} RH, sharper than "no gaps").\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{../B2-THEOREM.md} --- \textbf{PATH (A) CLOSED: the complete B-2 theorem.} Self-contained:
\end{itemize}
  Lemmas A/B/C/D + depth split all \textbf{unconditional}; the residual \textbf{hypothesis (H)} (uniform short-interval\par
  zero-density, \ensuremath{\ll} RH) precisely isolated. **Theorem: modulo (H), a faithful semibounded $\mathcal T$ exists,\par
  RH \ensuremath{\iff} sign of its bottom.** Ready to validate.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \texttt{../RH-ENDGAME.md} --- RH end-game: B-2 = finite bottom; RH = the SIGN (structural
\end{itemize}
  positivity $\mathcal T=A^*A$), untouched by the magnitude machinery.\par

| \textbf{B-2 plausibly UNCONDITIONAL} | $\kappa(b)\le e^d$ uniform (band-limited, $|b|<\tfrac12<d$); off-line via classical zero-density \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\widetilde{\mathfrak t}_-\le C\mathfrak t_+$ finite \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\mathfrak t\ge(1-4C)\|\cdot\|^2_{H_+}$. \textbf{Montgomery NOT needed} | Day20 ?3--4 | $\blacklozenge$ to-audit |\par
| \textbf{Proofs A/B/C} | IBP valid in $PW_d\cap H^1$ [OK]; $E_g=O(\mathfrak t_+)$ (Bernstein+Selberg, $O$ not $o$) [OK]; vertical $\|F(\cdot+ib)\|^2\le e^d\|F\|^2$ exact [OK] | Day21 ?1 | [OK] verified |\par

\subsection*{Chronology}

\subsection*{2026-06-01 --- Day 0.}
Opened the workspace. Pinned $(\mathcal H,\mathcal T)$ (A.0). Two threads\par
started in parallel per the work program ?7:\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Problem A.} Reduced the compression identity to two analytic facts: (i) the localizers lie in
\end{itemize}
  the form domain (A.1/A.2), (ii) the finite-cutoff computed matrix converges to the exact form entries\par
  (A.4 = P7-B restated). With both, $Q=P_J\mathcal T P_J$ is essentially a *tautology of the Gram\par
  matrix* --- A is the most decidable problem, as predicted. Remaining: tighten the archimedean bound in\par
  A.1 and restate P7-B at operator-norm level (A.4).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Problem B-2.} Established the free part is bounded below (B2.1) and the prime form converges on
\end{itemize}
  Schwartz functions (B2.2). \textbf{Key finding of Day 0:} the naive functional-analytic route (KLMN /\par
  relative form-boundedness) \textbf{provably cannot work} (B2.3) --- the prime perturbation is "form-larger"\par
  than the log-growing archimedean part, so semiboundedness cannot come from soft perturbation theory.\par
  It must come from \textbf{arithmetic cancellation} in $\sum\Lambda(n)n^{-1/2}T_{\log n}$, i.e. from the\par
  distribution of primes/zeros. \textbf{This is the mechanism behind the ?3.3 conjecture} that B-2 sits at\par
  "zero-density level," now derived rather than asserted.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-0 headline.} A is on track to be genuinely provable. B-2's difficulty has been *localized*:\par
it is not soft analysis, it is a single explicit inequality (B2.4) tying the negative prime form to\par
the archimedean form, whose constant is controlled by zero density. The frontier is now one boxed\par
inequality, not a vague "entanglement."\par
\end{quote}

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 1.}
Two referee alerts on the Day-0 ?5, both conceded, both load-bearing:\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Alert 1.} The "multiplier symbol" $\Phi(r)=2\sum\Lambda(n)n^{-1/2}\cos(r\log n)$ and
\end{itemize}
  $\inf_r(\Omega-\Phi)$ were illegitimate: the prime measure $\nu$ has mass $\asymp e^{t/2}$ per unit\par
  interval, so it is \textbf{non-tempered} and $\Phi=\widehat\nu$ is \textbf{not} a tempered distribution. (SB) had\par
  to be restated as a \textbf{distributional pairing on the positive-type cone} $\{|\widehat g|^2\}$, never a\par
  pointwise bound. The pairing exists only on the strip-width-$>\tfrac12$ class --- the *same* class the\par
  pole forced in A. *(B2 ?5.1.)*\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Alert 2.} "Finitely many off-line zeros $\Rightarrow$ (SB)" is \textbf{not} a corollary. An off-line
\end{itemize}
  quartet's factors $\widehat g(a\pm ib)=\int g\,e^{\mp bu}e^{-iau}du$ are point-evaluations **off the\par
  real axis\textbf{, which are }unbounded functionals on $L^2(\mathbb R,du)$** ($e^{\mp bu}\notin L^2$). So one\par
  off-line zero already makes the form a-priori unbounded; finiteness proves nothing. *(B2 ?5.3.)*\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Day-1 finding (what the corrections destapan).} The Hilbert-space \textbf{norm} --- invisible to Problem A
\end{itemize}
  --- is what decides B-2. With naive $L^2$, off-axis evaluations are unbounded and (SB) **plausibly\par
  collapses to RH** (no separation). The genuine-weakening branch *requires* a weighted reproducing-kernel\par
  norm --- a \textbf{de Branges space $H(E)$} in which strip point-evaluations are bounded. **So B and D are the\par
  same problem viewed twice:\textbf{ B2.4a (find the norm) }is** de Branges step (i). Corrects Day-0's "no free\par
  $\delta$": no free parameter for identity A, but the \textbf{norm/weight is a genuine, decisive choice for B-2}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{v10 reframed:} "measure $\inf_r(\Omega-\Phi_X)$" is only heuristic (no such inf); the rigorous probe
\end{itemize}
  is form-level $\inf\mathfrak t(g,g)/\|g\|_{H(E)}^2$ with sensitivity-to-weight testing.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-1 headline.} The entanglement is now concrete and *located in the norm*: B-2 is well-posed only\par
in a de Branges space, and there it splits into B2.4a (construct $E$ so strip evaluations are bounded)\par
+ B2.4b (the zero-density inequality). Merge the B and D sub-teams. Next: build $E_{T_0,\sigma}$ and\par
read Bombieri's norm.\par
\end{quote}

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 2.}
Followed the directive "pursue B/de Branges while hot" (do \textbf{not} stop to write\par
up A first). Attacked B2.4a directly. Results in \texttt{B2.4a-de-branges-norm.md}:\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DB.1 [OK]} The free part is the Gamma geometry: $\Omega(r)=2\,\mathrm{Re}(\gamma'/\gamma)(\tfrac12+ir)$,
\end{itemize}
  $\gamma(s)=\pi^{-s/2}\Gamma(s/2)$. The ambient space of B is forced --- it is $\gamma$'s de Branges space.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DB.2 [OK]} Width-$\tfrac12$ \textbf{triple coincidence}: the admissible strip ($>\tfrac12$, from the pole),
\end{itemize}
  the off-line displacement range ($|\beta-\tfrac12|<\tfrac12$), and $\gamma(\tfrac12+iz)$'s first pole\par
  ($z=i/2$) are the \textbf{same strip}. Three independently-arrived constants collapse to one.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DB.3 \$\textbackslash{}blacklozenge\$} In any de Branges $H(E)$, point-evaluations are bounded at \textbf{every} $w\in\mathbb C$
\end{itemize}
  (reproducing kernel $K_w$) --- so the Day-1 $L^2$ pathology (off-axis evals unbounded) simply **does not\par
  occur**. A space with bounded strip evaluations *exists* --- the archimedean de Branges space of $\gamma$.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DB.4 --- the catch and the consolidation.} The de Branges weight $|E|^{-2}\asymp e^{\pi|r|/2}$ is
\end{itemize}
  \textbf{exponentially stronger} than the Weil energy $\Omega\sim\log|r|$. Positivity ($=$RH) is\par
  norm-independent but \textbf{semiboundedness is norm-dependent}, and the strong norm makes it *easier*\par
  (good) while \textbf{redefining the Rayleigh quotient the ladder converges to} (so $E$ is now a shared\par
  parameter of B *and* C). No single $E$ does both "bound evaluations" (strong norm) and "be the Weil\par
  form" (weak $\log$ norm); the principled reconciliation is the de Branges \textbf{chain} $\{H(E_a)\}$. **?\par
  HEADLINE: B-2(b) $\equiv$ the de Branges chain/ordering condition for $E_{T_0,\sigma}$ $\equiv$ (LB).**\par
  Every flank now points at one object ($E_{T_0,\sigma}$) and one condition. v9's "no Conrey--Li" is\par
  re-priced as *direct* evidence about that chain condition.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-2 headline.} The program consolidated. B fully merges into D; the named inequality (LB) is now\par
*literally* a de Branges chain condition for a Gamma-factor-based localized $E_{T_0,\sigma}$. The spine\par
of Phase 4 (DB-open) is: (1) construct $E_{T_0,\sigma}$; (2) write the chain/ordering condition;\par
(3) prove it (conditionally on zero density) and confirm Conrey--Li immunity in the localized regime.\par
A stays in write-up; B/D is the live frontier.\par
\end{quote}

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 3.}
Referee gave two corrections on Day 2, both conceded, both load-bearing; the\par
second produced the day's real content. Record in \texttt{B2.4a-closability.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Correction A --- \texttt{\textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}equiv\}} was overstated.} Day-2's "B-2 $\equiv$ de Branges chain condition" is only
\end{itemize}
  $\rightsquigarrow$ (suggestive). Upgrading needs three unproven things: (1) $H(E)$ canonical, (2) the\par
  Weil spectral bottom preserved on passing to the chain, (3) semiboundedness $\iff$ ordering. Downgraded\par
  everywhere.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item **Correction B --- the deep worry: does a strong norm *trivialize* the instability?** If the de Branges
\end{itemize}
  weight is exponential, the archimedean form becomes negligible (CL ?1) and semiboundedness could be\par
  vacuous --- a property of the space, not of $\zeta$. Valid risk.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{My self-catch (prompted by B).} Day-2's weight asymptotic $|E|^{-2}\asymp e^{\pi|r|/2}$ was
\end{itemize}
  \textbf{asserted, not verified} --- I conflated the *modulus* $|\gamma|$ (exponential) with the de Branges\par
  *density of states* $\varphi'\sim\log$ (logarithmic). Which one is the weight \textbf{gates the whole worry}\par
  (CL ?0): exponential \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} trivialization real; logarithmic \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} norm $\approx$ Weil energy, no trivialization.\par
  Flagged ??, not built upon. (Exactly the $\Phi$-type slip, caught early this time.)\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{The contribution (CL ?2) --- sign/value invariance principle.} "$\inf\operatorname{spec}\ge0$" $=$ RH
\end{itemize}
  is \textbf{norm-independent} (it never mentions the inner product); only *finiteness* of the bottom is\par
  norm-dependent. So the norm can corrupt the \textbf{value} (B-2) but \textbf{never the sign} (RH). Closability is\par
  exactly the guarantee that the sign *transfers to the completion*. This both answers the referee\par
  (RH cannot be hidden by the norm) and vindicates the directive (closability is the precise bridge).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Reduction (CL ?3).} Closability of $\mathfrak t$ in $H(E)$ $\iff$ one rigorous, distribution-free
\end{itemize}
  inequality (C-bound): the \textbf{$H(E)$-relative KLMN bound on $\mathfrak p$} --- the same bound that *failed*\par
  in $L^2$ (B2.3), now re-asked in the stronger norm where it may hold; an inequality between the prime\par
  measure $\nu$ and the de Branges weight $|E|^{-2}$.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Trichotomy (CL ?4).} Verdict is one of: (1) closable \& non-trivially bounded below \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} faithful ladder
\end{itemize}
  well-posed (best); (2) closable but trivially bounded \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} B-2 vacuous, content reverts to sign$=$RH (no\par
  separation); (3) not closable \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} wrong space (referee's worry realized). All three are informative.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-3 headline.} Reprioritized per referee: \textbf{do not build $E_{T_0,\sigma}$ yet.} Order is\par
(0) verify the archimedean de Branges \textbf{weight asymptotic} (log vs exp --- one literature computation,\par
gates all), (1) decide \textbf{closability} via (C-bound), reading Bombieri's norm, (2) only if case 1 holds,\par
construct the chain. The sign/value principle guarantees no choice of norm can fake or hide RH; the open\par
risk is whether a *faithful* (closable, non-trivial) norm exists at all. Immediate next computation: ?0.\par
\end{quote}

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 4.}
Per referee directive ("actively try to break DB.4 before building it").\par
Record in \texttt{B2.4a-break-attempt.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{CL.0 resolved (double self-correction).} The de Branges \textbf{norm weight is exponential}
\end{itemize}
  $|E|^{-2}\asymp e^{\pi|x|/2}$ (Day-2 instinct was right); the \textbf{density of states $\sim\log$} is a\par
  *different* object (Day-3 caught a real object but mislabeled it the norm). We are in the strong-norm\par
  regime; trivialization worry is live \ensuremath{\to} test it.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{THE BREAK (BR.1).} Tried to falsify semiboundedness in $H(E_\gamma)$ --- and \textbf{succeeded}. Scaling
\end{itemize}
  family $\widehat g_\varepsilon$ = bump of width $\varepsilon\to0$ at fixed $T_0$ (wide-in-$u$): the\par
  norm $\asymp e^{\pi|T_0|/2}\|\widehat g\|_{L^2}^2$ depends on \textbf{location} $T_0$, *blind to width*\par
  $\varepsilon$; but the prime form $\asymp\|\widehat g\|_{L^2}^2\cdot e^{1/2\varepsilon}$ (Chebyshev\par
  $\sum_{n\le N}\Lambda(n)n^{-1/2}\sim2\sqrt N$, $N=e^{1/\varepsilon}$). So\par
  $\mathfrak t/\|g\|_{H(E)}^2\sim -e^{1/2\varepsilon}\to-\infty$. **$\mathfrak t$ is NOT semibounded in\par
  the pure de Branges space of $\gamma$.** An amplitude-by-location weight cannot control a width-driven\par
  divergence. \textbf{DB.4-as-stated is falsified.}\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Consistency (BR.2).} Band-limited ($PW_\tau$) test functions $\Rightarrow$ $\mathfrak p$ a finite
\end{itemize}
  sum $\Rightarrow$ bounded (classical "tame on band-limited" Weil/Bombieri--Lagarias regime); the blow-up\par
  uses the opposite wide-in-$u$ regime --- no contradiction, and it locates RH content in the\par
  non-band-limited limit. v9 (fixed $\sigma$, grow $J$) explored a *different* direction than the\par
  blow-up ($\sigma\to0$); \textbf{v10 falsifiable prediction:} $\sigma\to0$ scan $\Rightarrow\lambda_{\min}\to-\infty$\par
  in $L^2$ normalization.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Redirection (BR.3).} Faithful norm must control \textbf{amplitude (location)} AND \textbf{width/smoothness}.
\end{itemize}
  That is a \textbf{Fock/Bargmann (Gaussian phase-space)} norm --- whose ON basis is the **Hermite functions =\par
  our localizers**. The program's Gaussian window was secretly the right geometry; de Branges (DB.1--DB.3)\par
  survives as the *location half*. The chain picture is replaced by a Gaussian phase-space picture.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-4 headline.} Trying to break DB.4 broke it --- cleanly and usefully. The pure de Branges space is\par
*not* the faithful home (Weil form unbounded below there, explicit width-driven $\sqrt N$ blow-up). The\par
same calculation redirects to \textbf{Fock/Bargmann}, the natural home of the Hermite--Gauss instrument, as\par
the candidate that can bound both off-line evaluations and the prime form. Next: (1) make BR.1 rigorous;\par
(2) write $\mathcal T$ in the Bargmann transform and test whether the Fock norm cures the blow-up; (3)\par
v10 $\sigma\to0$ falsifier. $E_{T_0,\sigma}$ deferred (was for the superseded picture).\par
\textbf{[Day-4 headline is itself retracted --- see Day 5.]}\par
\end{quote}

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 5. [X] RETRACTION of BR.1 (and B2.3).}
Attempting (per referee) to make BR.1 rigorous\par
*before* building the Fock formalism revealed BR.1 is \textbf{false}. Record in \texttt{B2.4a-break-attempt.md} ?5.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{The disproof (explicit-formula identity, EF-id).} $\mathfrak t(g,g)=\mathfrak a+\mathfrak q-\mathfrak p=\sum_\rho|\widehat g(\gamma_\rho)|^2$
\end{itemize}
  is an \textbf{identity}. For a smooth bump $\widehat g_\varepsilon$ of width $\varepsilon\to0$ at a generic\par
  $T_0$, the right side counts only zeros within $\varepsilon$ --- \textbf{finite, $\to0$}. So $\mathfrak p$ is\par
  \textbf{finite}, not $\sim e^{1/2\varepsilon}$. The $\sqrt N$ "blow-up" was an artifact of the \textbf{hard cutoff}\par
  $\mathbf 1_{\log n\le1/\varepsilon}$ the referee flagged as non-innocent; the smooth test function\par
  \textbf{resums} the pointwise-divergent prime series to $\Phi(T_0)=2\,\mathrm{Re}(-\zeta'/\zeta(\tfrac12+iT_0))$,\par
  finite. The predicted oscillatory cancellation is exactly what kills it.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Scope.} BR.1 [X] withdrawn; BR.3 (Fock pivot) [X] withdrawn (rested on BR.1); **B2.3 (Day 0) used the
\end{itemize}
  SAME hard-cutoff error** --- its "$\mathfrak p\gg\mathfrak a$" is not established (by EF-id, $\mathfrak p$\par
  is *comparable* to $\mathfrak a$). CL.0 [OK], DB.1--DB.3 [OK], Day-1 off-axis mechanism [OK] all survive.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Corrected picture --- $H(E_\gamma)$ is BACK IN PLAY.} The only rigorous $L^2$ unboundedness is Day-1's:
\end{itemize}
  off-line zero $\Rightarrow$ off-axis evaluation $\Rightarrow$ unbounded on $L^2$, but **bounded in\par
  $H(E_\gamma)$ (DB.3)**. So B-2 in $H(E_\gamma)$ $\rightsquigarrow$ "is $\sum_{\text{off-line}}$(bounded\par
  terms) bounded below?" $=$ \textbf{zero-density} $=$ exactly ?3.3's original conjecture, now reached cleanly\par
  with the prime-blow-up phantom removed. The Day-2/3/4 chain/Fock detours were chasing an artifact.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Meta-lesson (logged permanently).} The hard-cutoff-of-a-conditionally-convergent-series error
\end{itemize}
  appeared Day 0 AND Day 4 and survived four passes. \textbf{Mandatory rule:} every blow-up claim must be\par
  checked against EF-id ($\mathfrak t=\sum_\rho|\widehat g(\gamma_\rho)|^2$) before being believed.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-5 headline.} A clean self-retraction, the program's ethos working. The "break" was the artifact,\par
not the de Branges space. After five days the picture \textbf{converges back to ?3.3}: B-1 unconditional\par
(von Neumann); B-2 well-posed in the archimedean de Branges space $H(E_\gamma)$ (off-axis evaluations\par
bounded, DB.3), reducing to a \textbf{zero-density inequality} on the off-line-zero sum. No Fock, no chain\par
required by the evidence. Next: (1) B-2 as a zero-density problem in $H(E_\gamma)$; (2) Bombieri's norm;\par
(3) re-examine whether any genuine norm-dependence survives. The instrument's recurring temptation ---\par
manufacturing blow-ups by hard-truncating --- is now a named, guarded-against failure mode.\par
\end{quote}

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 6. Audit of EF-id (the new pillar) --- survives, with two corrections.}
Per referee:\par
before building on EF-id, audit it (three questions). Record in \texttt{EF-identity-audit.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Q3 (role of RH): Case A, unconditional.} (EF) is the Weil explicit formula --- a theorem, no RH input.
\end{itemize}
  RH enters only in the *sign* of the (unconditional) RHS. \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} using EF-id to refute BR.1 is legitimate; it\par
  is NOT circular. [OK]\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Q2 (is the RHS positive?): NO --- notation corrected.} $\mathfrak t(g,g)=\sum_\rho h(\gamma_\rho)$ with
\end{itemize}
  $h=\widehat g\,\widehat g^*$. On-line zeros give $|\widehat g(\gamma)|^2\ge0$; **off-line quartets give\par
  $4\,\mathrm{Re}[\widehat g(t-ib)^2]$ --- INDEFINITE**, built from off-axis evaluations. Positivity $\iff$\par
  RH (Weil's criterion). The Day-5 shorthand "$\sum|\widehat g(\gamma_\rho)|^2$" was valid only under RH;\par
  fixed everywhere.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Q1 (domain): the real frontier.} (EF) holds \textbf{unconditionally on $C_c^\infty$ and on $\mathcal D$}
\end{itemize}
  (dense core); whether it \textbf{and the sign survive the $H(E_\gamma)$-closure is OPEN} --- an identity on a\par
  dense core need not control the closure (the referee's deep point). EF-id is [OK] \textbf{core-level}, ? closure.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  On-line part $\ge0$; off-line part = bounded $H(E)$-evals (DB.3) \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} \textbf{zero-density} question (?3.3).\par

\end{itemize}
  evaluations) is a \textbf{non-decreasing supremum of bounded closed forms}, hence \textbf{closed} by **Kato's\par
  monotone convergence theorem for forms**. \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} a non-negative self-adjoint operator $T_+\ge0$ on\par
  $H(E_\gamma)$ exists \textbf{unconditionally} (B-1 concrete + positive half of B-2, no hypotheses).\par

  numerics live in.** de Branges geometry vindicated; chain/Fock detours unnecessary.\par

\end{itemize}
  $|\mathfrak t_-(g)|\le a\,\mathfrak t_+(g)+C\|g\|^2$, $a<1$ (KLMN). It is a **zero-density comparison of\par

\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  (Stirling on $|E_\gamma|\asymp|\gamma|$), so $\operatorname{Tr}T_+=\sum_\gamma K(\gamma,\gamma)<\infty$\par
  \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} \textbf{$\mathfrak t_+$ (and $\mathfrak t_-$) BOUNDED} \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\mathfrak t$ bounded \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} CLOS.1/CLOS.2 are\par

  space (the Gamma one, exp. weight $e^{\pi|t|/2}$ --- that's the space *of the Gamma factor*, NOT *of the\par
  archimedean energy* $\mathfrak a$ whose weight is only $\Omega\sim\log$).\par

\end{itemize}
  evals $|b|<\tfrac12$ bounded (RKHS of strip; $\epsilon$ fits the pole at $\pm i/2$); (2) \textbf{non-trivial}\par

  $t$-flat, edge-blowup. ($\epsilon$ = the regularization; deep zeros $|b|\to\tfrac12$ near edge = dangerous.)\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  (infinitely many off-line). So $a=0$ (Day-8 B.2) cannot hold; \textbf{relative Carleson ($a>0$) FORCED} ---\par
  a classical Carleson-measure problem for $H^2(S_d)$, fine zero-geometry ($S(T)$, separation), NOT raw\par
  density. Exactly the referee's prediction ("$S_{\mathrm{off}}<\infty$ hides almost all the difficulty").\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  A.2 re-posed: zeros over-sample ($\log T$ density vs $H^2(S_d)$ flat) \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} possible lower frame bound;\par
  flat-vs-log weight is part of A.2.\par

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 11. AUDIT of the Day-10 theorem (new pillar) --- TWO gaps found, reconstructed.}
The\par
referee chose to re-audit the Day-10 theorem before advancing. Record in\par
\texttt{Day11-theorem-audit.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{F2 gap CONCEDED [X] (referee's catch).} "faithful $\Rightarrow\inf_t K(t,t)>0$" is \textbf{FALSE}:
\end{itemize}
  $K\sim1/\log t$ gives $\sum_\gamma K(\gamma,\gamma)\sim\sum_n 1/\log n=\infty$ (faithful) yet $\inf K=0$.\par
  Solid one-liner is only \textbf{$\inf_t K(t,t)>0\Rightarrow S_{\mathrm{off}}=\infty$}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{F1 gap FOUND \$\textbackslash{}blacklozenge\$ (this audit).} Expansion $K(t-ib,t-ib)=K(t,t)+b^2 D(t)+\dots$, $D(t)=\sum_n(e_n'^2-e_ne_n'')$,
\end{itemize}
  and $D(t)$ \textbf{can be $<0$} (a function with $e'(t)=0,e''(t)>0$). So F1 ($K$ larger off-axis) is **not\par
  universal\textbf{ --- holds for }translation-invariant** spaces (convex even $\kappa(b)$, min at 0) but not\par
  generally. The Day-10 "space-independent" label was wrong; it's structure-dependent.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{RECONSTRUCTED density-adapted theorem [OK]/\$\textbackslash{}blacklozenge\$ (referee's suggestion, precised):} (i) $K(t,t)\ge c/\log(2+|t|)$
\end{itemize}
  + (ii) F1 + (iii) off-line positive proportion ($\sum_{\text{off-line}}1/\log t_\rho=\infty$) $\Rightarrow$\par
  $S_{\mathrm{off}}\ge c\sum_{\text{off-line}}1/\log t_\rho=\infty$ $\Rightarrow$ $a=0$ impossible. Covers\par
  BOTH candidate spaces (flat strip Hardy: $K=$const; log-weighted: $K\sim1/\log$); needs no constant kernel.\par
  (i) is a mild extra regularity beyond bare faithfulness = the referee's $K\gtrsim1/\log$ threshold.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{META-FRAME (referee's point): structural-constraint / impossibility list K1--K4} --- the durable output
\end{itemize}
  is NOT a space but constraints any faithful realization must satisfy (K1 trivial$\perp$faithful; K2\par
  faithful$\perp a=0$; K3 Gamma-dB excluded; K4 strong-norm$\perp$nontrivial). Impossibility results\par
  survive model changes better than positive constructions.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-11 headline.} The new pillar got the hard audit it deserved: \textbf{both} F1 and F2 had gaps, so the\par
"space-independent theorem" is downgraded to a **density-adapted impossibility result with explicit\par
hypotheses** (i)--(iii) --- still covering the candidate spaces, still forcing relative Carleson. The\par

relative-Carleson difficulty is unavoidable inside it. Methodological shift (referee): we are now\par

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 12. THE DENSITY SCALING LAW (referee: reformulate via $\rho(t)$, classify F1).}
Both\par
asks fused into the deepest result so far. Record in \texttt{Day12-density-scaling-law.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DENS.1 --- faithfulness criterion, $\inf K$-free [OK]/\$\textbackslash{}blacklozenge\$:} replacing $\sum_\gamma$ by $\int(\cdot)\rho\,dt$
\end{itemize}
  ($S(T)$ fluctuation lower-order for slowly-varying $K$): \textbf{FAITHFUL $\iff K(t,t)\rho(t)\notin L^1$}.\par
  Verifies the 3 cases (flat $K\rho\sim\log\to\infty$; log $K\rho\sim1$; Gamma $K\rho\in L^1$ trivial). This\par
  is the referee's exact $K\gtrsim1/\log$ threshold, and it \textbf{removes the Day-11 F2 gap} (no $\inf K$).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DENS.2 --- F1 CLASSIFIED = Level B geometric [OK]:} kernel identity $K(t-ib,t-ib)=K(t,t)+b^2D+\dots$ with
\end{itemize}
  $D=2K_{11}-\tfrac12K''=K_{11}-\sum e_ne_n''$ ($K_{11}=\sum e_n'^2\ge0$), double-checked via $\Delta K=4K_{11}$.\par
  \textbf{F1 $\iff K''(t)\le4K_{11}(t)$}, and for a density-matched (slowly-varying) diagonal \$K''\textbackslash{}sim K/t\textasciicircum{}2\textbackslash{}lll\par
  K\_\{11\}\textbackslash{}sim K/d\textasciicircum{}2\$, so F1 holds --- a consequence of \textbf{band geometry}, NOT translation-invariance, NOT\par
  accidental. Resolves the referee's "model vs problem" risk in the GOOD direction. Verified on explicit\par
  strip kernel ($K_{11}=\pi^2/16d^3>0$).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DENS.4 --- NECESSARY SCALING LAW [OK]/\$\textbackslash{}blacklozenge\$ (the durable, model-independent output):} any faithful realization
\end{itemize}
  obeys $K\rho\notin L^1$; canonical = critical sampling $K\asymp1/\rho\sim2\pi/\log t$ ($R=K\rho\asymp1$).\par
  Bonus: \textbf{even $H(E_\xi)$ (full $\xi$ de Branges) trivializes} ($|E|\sim e^{-\pi t/4}$ \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $K\rho\in L^1$),\par
  so the faithful space is NOT a standard de Branges space ($|E|$ decaying) --- needs $|E|\asymp$const\par
  (Hardy-band). K2 in density form: $S_{\mathrm{off}}=\infty\iff K\rho_{\mathrm{off}}\notin L^1$.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{POSITIVE ADVANCE --- form-core A.2 = a sampling problem [OK](reduction):} in the critical space
\end{itemize}
  $\mu_{\mathrm{on}}$ is \textbf{Carleson} (1 zero/box) \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} \textbf{UPPER frame bound PROVED} ($\mathfrak t_+$ bounded,\par
  non-trace-class = "bounded but not trace-class," correcting Day-9's loose "unbounded"). Then **A.2\par
  $\Leftarrow$ LOWER frame bound $\iff\{\gamma\}$ a SAMPLING sequence for $H_{\mathrm{crit}}$** --- a\par
  Beurling-borderline question (holds under RH: zeros = de Branges Riesz basis of $H(E_\xi)$; uncond. open).\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-12 headline.} The referee's "reformulate via density" produced the program's deepest pure-math\par

\subsection*{2026-06-02 --- Day 13. AUDIT of DENS.1 (the new pillar; referee priority over the lower-frame-bound).}
The\par
sum$\to$integral step rests on $\int K\,dS$ being lower-order. Record in\par
\texttt{Day13-DENS1-audit.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{The fluctuation computation (referee's concern, done):} $E(T)=\int_0^T K\,dS=K(T)S(T)-\int_0^T SK'\,dt$,
\end{itemize}
  bounded via crude $|S|=O(\log)$. Rates: flat $E=O(\log T)$ vs $M\asymp T\log T$; critical $E\asymp\int\frac{dt}{t\log t}=O(\log\log T)$\par
  vs $M\asymp T$; near-boundary $E$ \textbf{converges} vs $M\asymp\log\log T$; Gamma both converge. **The referee\par
  is right that $\int\frac{dt}{t\log t}=\infty$ (error diverges) --- but at rate $\log\log T\lll T\sim M$, so\par
  $E=o(M)$ always; converges near the faithfulness boundary where the verdict is decided.** Sign harmless\par
  ($M\to+\infty$). The verdict $K\rho\in L^1$? never flips.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{VERDICT (matches referee's prediction): DENS.1 HOLDS, now CONDITIONED:} $K$ \textbf{regularly varying}
\end{itemize}
  ($|K'|/K\lesssim1/t$, no wild oscillation) $\Rightarrow$ [faithful $\iff K\rho\notin L^1$]. Mild, met by\par
  ALL band candidates (flat, critical). \textbf{Crude $S=O(\log)$ suffices --- no fine $S(t)$ input, no RH.} The\par
  \textbf{critical scaling law $K\asymp1/\rho$ survives UNCONDITIONALLY} (independent of the $S$-audit).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{META: first audited pillar (Days 7--13) to HOLD UP} --- only acquired an honest side-condition, didn't
\end{itemize}
  crack (unlike CLOS-in-$H(E_\gamma)$, the Day-10 theorem). Possible sign of reaching stable ground.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-13 headline.} The referee's audit of the new pillar was right to demand and \textbf{favorable}: DENS.1\par
survives with its hypothesis made explicit ("$K$ regularly varying") exactly as predicted --- a genuine but\par
mild conditioning, needing nothing delicate about $S(t)$. The divergent-but-slower fluctuation\par
($\log\log T\lll T$) is the precise resolution of the "$\int dt/(t\log t)=\infty$" worry. Durable stack:\par

**2026-06-02 --- Day 14. AUDIT of the "A.2 $\Leftarrow$ lower frame bound" reduction (referee Priority 1) ---\par
finds a SECOND TRIVIALITY.** Record in \texttt{Day14-reduction-audit.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{THE HOLE [X]:} Day-12 ?6 did the reduction in the \textbf{critical space} ($R=K\rho\asymp1$). There
\end{itemize}
  $\mu_{\mathrm{on}}$ Carleson \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\mathfrak t_+$ \textbf{bounded} \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} form-core AUTOMATIC (no frame bound needed).\par
  BUT $\mu_{\mathrm{off}}$ (same critical density, interior depths) also Carleson \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\mathfrak t_-$ bounded\par
  \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\mathfrak t$ \textbf{BOUNDED} \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} \textbf{B-2 VACUOUS}. So the critical space is a \textbf{2nd triviality T2} (distinct\par
  from Day-9 trace-class T1): T1 = $K\rho\in L^1$ ($\mathfrak t_+$ compact); T2 = $\mu$ Carleson / $R$\par
  bounded ($\mathfrak t$ bounded, B-2 vacuous). Days 12--13 treated critical $R\asymp1$ as canonical --- it's\par
  \textbf{T2-trivial}. Referee's Priority-1 audit caught it.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{CORRECTION [OK]:} genuine (non-vacuous) B-2 needs $\mathfrak t$ unbounded-below-able \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\mathfrak t_-$
\end{itemize}
  unbounded \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\mu_{\mathrm{off}}$ NOT Carleson \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} over-sampling \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} \textbf{$R=K\rho\to\infty$}. The genuine\par
  faithful space is \textbf{flat (sub-critical-weight) Hardy-band}, $R\sim\log t\to\infty$, where $\mathfrak t_\pm$\par
  are UNBOUNDED. Sharpened ladder: T1 ($\in L^1$) / T2 ($R$ bounded, incl. critical) / genuine ($R\to\infty$).\par
  "faithful $\Rightarrow K\rho\notin L^1$" still necessary but NOT sufficient (critical satisfies it yet\par
  T2-trivial); genuine needs strictly stronger $R\to\infty$. \textbf{New constraint K5: bounded $\perp$ genuine B-2.}\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{A.2 \textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}ne\} frame bound in the genuine space [OK]:} with $R\to\infty$, $\mathfrak t_+$ unbounded, and upper bound
\end{itemize}
  (Carleson) FAILS, lower bound (coercivity) and form-core (A.2) SEPARATE. The Day-12 ?6 reduction conflated\par
  form-core with coercivity. \textbf{Priority-2 bonus:} coercivity $T_+\ge c>0$ is the EASY part (over-dense zeros,\par
  Beurling lower density $\to\infty>$ Nyquist, modulo finite-rank low-$t$ correction). The genuine difficulty\par
  is (a) form-core density + (b) RFB $\mathfrak t_-\lesssim\mathfrak t_+$ (off-line$\le$on-line over-dense\par
  measures) --- both governed by FINE zero geometry (separation, $S(T)$, pair correlation), as the referee\par
  foresaw. So the classical input that enters is NOT Beurling density (gives coercivity free) but the finer\par
  relative comparison.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-14 headline.} Priority-1 audit of the reduction found a real Day-10-style hole: the "A.2 $\Leftarrow$\par
lower frame bound" was done in the critical space, which is a **second triviality (T2): $\mathfrak t$\par
bounded \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} B-2 vacuous\textbf{. Genuine B-2 lives in the }over-sampling** regime $R=K\rho\to\infty$ (flat\par

**2026-06-02 --- Day 15. AUDIT of K5 (referee: audit before pillarizing) --- the Carleson step CONFLATED TWO\par
INVARIANTS.** Record in \texttt{Day15-K5-audit.md}. Followed the referee's 3-step recipe.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Intrinsic resolution $\ell(t)=\sqrt{K(t,t)/K_{11}(t)}$} (kernel coherence length). For Hardy-band
\end{itemize}
  $\ell\asymp d$ \textbf{constant} (verified on explicit kernel: $\ell=2d/\pi$); slowly-varying weight doesn't\par
  change it (bandwidth set by strip width $d$, not weight).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Carleson is governed by $P=\rho\ell$, NOT $R=K\rho$ [OK].} $R/P=\sqrt{KK_{11}}\asymp K/d$; they coincide
\end{itemize}
  only when $K\asymp d$ (flat). For the "critical" weight $K\sim1/\log$: $R\asymp1$ \textbf{but} \$P=\textbackslash{}rho\textbackslash{}ell\textbackslash{}sim\par
  d\textbackslash{}log t\textbackslash{}to\textbackslash{}infty$. **So "$R\textbackslash{}asymp1\textbackslash{}Rightarrow\textbackslash{}mu\$ Carleson" (the K5 step) is FALSE** --- the critical-weight\par
  space over-samples ($P\to\infty$), $\mathfrak t_+$ unbounded, NOT T2-trivial. Exactly the referee's\par
  "which spatial scale?" concern.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Over-sampling is FORCED for all admissible spaces [OK].} Eval-bounding at depth $\tfrac12$ $\Rightarrow$
\end{itemize}
  $d\ge\tfrac12$ $\Rightarrow$ $\ell\gtrsim\tfrac12$ $\Rightarrow$ $P=\rho\ell\gtrsim\tfrac12\rho\to\infty$.\par
  So every eval-bounding strip space over-samples; $\mathfrak t_+$ \textbf{always unbounded}. \textbf{No T2 there.} The\par
  only Carleson ($P\asymp1$) spaces are resolution-shrinking ($\ell\sim1/\log$) = de Branges ($\varphi'\sim\log$),\par
  but those have $|E|$ decaying \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} \textbf{T1 (trace-class)}. T2 (Carleson+faithful) needs $\varphi'\sim\log$ with\par
  $|E|\asymp$const --- blocked by the HB phase--amplitude relation; \textbf{likely collapses into T1}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{VERDICT:} \textbf{K5 downgraded \$\textbackslash{}blacklozenge\$} (not established; no T2 among admissible spaces). **Day-14 conclusion
\end{itemize}
  SURVIVES with a stronger reason:\textbf{ genuine = over-sampling Hardy-band is }forced** ($\ell\ge\tfrac12$),\par
  not contingent on a T2 dichotomy. \textbf{DENS.1 unaffected} (it is the $R$/trace-class question, correct\par
  invariant). Durable gain: \textbf{clean separation $R=K\rho$ (trace-class) vs $P=\rho\ell$ (Carleson)} --- Day-14\par
  had merged them. "Critical scaling $K\asymp1/\rho$" is a trace-density normalization, NOT critical\par
  sampling (terminology corrected).\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-15 headline.} K5's audit (referee's call) caught a genuine invariant-conflation: Carleson depends\par
on $P=\rho\ell$ (resolution), not $R=K\rho$ (trace density); eval-boundedness forces $\ell\gtrsim\tfrac12$,\par
so over-sampling ($P\to\infty$) is \textbf{universal} among admissible spaces --- $\mathfrak t_+$ always\par
unbounded, genuine space forced. T2/K5 downgraded; the over-sampling conclusion upgraded from contingent\par

**2026-06-02 --- Day 16. Carleson sufficiency (Schur) + a rigorous reduction of RFB (referee provided a\par

\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  referee's argument); \textbf{full equivalence FALSE} (clustering breaks it) --- sufficient direction only, $P$ =\par
  natural local density. \textbf{Direct $P\to\infty\Rightarrow\mathfrak t_+$ unbounded} via kernel test\par
  $\langle k_t,Tk_t\rangle/\|k_t\|^2\approx K(t,t)P\to\infty$ --- \textbf{upgrades Day-15} (box heuristic \ensuremath{\to} rigorous),\par
  answering the referee's "prove non-Carleson directly?" --- yes.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  over-sampling (over-counts by $P\to\infty$ --- the forced over-sampling biting back); both $\sum|F'(\gamma)|^2$\par
  and $\mathfrak t_+$ carry the $P$ factor, only the *ratio* is bounded; routing through $\|F\|^2$ loses it.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{The clean fix (derivative-free) [OK](mod regularity):} off-axis$\to$on-axis via interpolation coeffs
\end{itemize}
  $F(\gamma+ib)=\sum_{\gamma'}c_{\gamma'}F(\gamma')$, then Schur \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} $\widetilde{\mathfrak t}_-\le CC'\mathfrak t_+$\par
  \textbf{if} the $c$ are $\ell^1$-Schur bounded (rows AND columns). So RFB needs \textbf{TWO} fine-geometry hypotheses\par
  (sampling + Schur regularity), not the one the sketch claimed.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{CONDITIONAL THEOREM (Day-16 C):} [bounded multiplicity + zeros a sampling sequence with Schur
\end{itemize}
  interpolation regularity] $\Rightarrow\mathfrak t_-\lesssim\mathfrak t_+\Rightarrow$ **Weil form semibounded\par
  (B-2)\textbf{. }The arithmetic frontier, located precisely:** the regularity hypothesis = zeros a REGULAR\par
  sampling sequence = minimum \textbf{separation} / $S(T)$ control / \textbf{Montgomery pair correlation} / \textbf{GUE}.\par
  Honest tension: zeros have NO positive uniform min gap (close pairs expected), so hyp. must be the\par
  *averaged/Schur* form --- itself a pair-correlation question. (Lower frame bound at over-critical density may\par
  still be RH-conditional --- the Day-12 ?6 loop persists, flagged.)\par

\begin{quote}\itshape

\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  = Montgomery sum, $\widehat r=\mathbf 1_{[-2d,2d]}$, scale $1/d$. **Form factor enters at $\beta=\xi/\rho\to0$\par

\end{itemize}
  fails, but in the \textbf{zero-sampling space $H_+\cong\ell^2(\{\gamma\})$} ($\mathfrak t_+=\|\cdot\|^2$),\par

  Over-sampling is *cured* by working in $H_+$ ($\mathcal T_+=I$). So B-2 reduces to quadrature + coercivity,\par
  not a direct RH proof.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  UNCONDITIONAL\textbf{ (counting), suff. }up to a $\log$**; off-diagonal $\log$ closed by Montgomery-range\par
  cancellation. \textbf{Decisive question: is $V$ bounded UNCONDITIONALLY?} If YES (BGSTB/Goldston--Montgomery/Gonek)\par

**2026-06-02 --- Day 22. Coercivity (?2\ensuremath{\tfrac12}) as PURE SAMPLING (referee: forget zeta, attack it as a frame\par
problem).** Record in \texttt{Day22-coercivity.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{?2\textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}tfrac12\} ANSWERED: $D^-=\infty$ does NOT give the lower frame bound [OK] (referee's instinct right).} Beurling:
\end{itemize}
  set of sampling for $PW_d$ $\Leftarrow$ no gap $>\pi/d$ (gap theorem); $D^-\ge d/\pi$ is NECESSARY not\par
  sufficient. A single Nyquist gap + a bump in it kills coercivity. **So the gap dependence is genuine, not\par
  removable by density.**\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{BUT the Day-21 "no gaps" framing was too crude.} Refinement: coercivity is **only needed near off-line
\end{itemize}
  zeros\textbf{ (a large gap with no off-line zeros is harmless, $\mathfrak t=\mathfrak t_+\ge0$). }DEPTH SPLIT:**\par
  shallow off-line ($|b|<\delta$, $\kappa\approx1$) sample like on-line --- \textbf{harmless} (may cluster); deep\par
  off-line ($|b|\ge\delta$, $\kappa$ up to $e^d$) are the danger but \textbf{locally $o(\rho)$} by classical\par
  \textbf{short-interval zero-density} ($N(\sigma,T+1)-N(\sigma,T)=o(\log T)$, $\sigma>\tfrac12$, uncond.). So every\par
  Nyquist window keeps $\sim P-o(P)$ samples with $\kappa\approx1$ \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} coercivity; deep part $=o(\mathfrak t_+)$.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{B-2 \textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}Leftarrow\} uniform short-interval zero-density for $\sigma>\tfrac12+\delta$} --- classical, plausibly
\end{itemize}
  unconditional, \textbf{\textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}ll\} RH, sharper than "no gaps".} TO EXECUTE: (1) pin $\delta$ + is the *uniform* (every $T$)\par
  short-interval density unconditional or only on-average? = THE frontier; (2) bound the shallow term; (3)\par
  rigorous coercivity from the $P-o(P)$ retained samples.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{RECALIBRATED:} \textasciitilde{}45\% uncond B-2 (down from \textasciitilde{}50\%), \textasciitilde{}35\% needs near-frontier uniform short-interval density,
\end{itemize}
  \textasciitilde{}20\% surprise. Lowered because the referee's coercivity worry was right --- it's NOT free from density.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-22 headline.} Attacking coercivity as pure sampling: \textbf{$D^-=\infty$ is insufficient} (one Nyquist\par
gap kills the lower frame bound --- the referee called it). But coercivity is only needed *near off-line\par
zeros*, and a \textbf{depth split} shows only \textbf{deep} off-line zeros (large $\kappa$) are dangerous --- and those\par
are \textbf{locally $o(\rho)$ by classical short-interval zero-density}, shallow ones harmless. So **B-2 \ensuremath{\Leftarrow}\par
uniform short-interval zero-density for $\sigma>\tfrac12$** --- sharper than the Day-21 "no gaps," \ensuremath{\ll} RH. Still\par
not a theorem: the *uniform* version of that density is the precise frontier. Next: is uniform short-interval\par
zero-density for fixed $\sigma>\tfrac12$ unconditional?\par
\end{quote}

  individually indefinite, NOT reflection-positive.**\par

  so geometry alone doesn't force the line; the Euler product does (confirms our Conj. B2); NCG/entropy = Connes\par
  = done (N4). None is the path, but PT-symmetry's *dynamical-attractor* instinct, made rigorous, IS.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Phase-8 path designed --- the de Bruijn--Newman heat flow.} RH $\iff\Lambda=0$ (Rodgers--Tao $\Lambda\ge0$;
\end{itemize}
  Polymath15 $\Lambda\le0.2$). \textbf{The escape from self-reference:} reality of zeros at $t\ge\Lambda>0$ is a\par
  THEOREM (not RH); propagating it back to $t=0$ is governed by the \textbf{Coulomb-gas ODE}, NOT the explicit\par
  formula --- so a dynamical/Lyapunov argument is not self-referential. The marginality $\Lambda=0$ = our measured\par
  $C\equiv1$ saturation. Synthesis: our detector measures $C(d,T_0;t)$ along the flow; B1's pair-correlation =\par
  the criticality. OpenAI-style methodology (precise lemmas, verify-first, self-refute, decision gates A/B/C).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Seed (Gate A) --- mechanism real \& measured; one guard-rail catch.} $C(t{=}0)=0.998\le1$ (marginal =
\end{itemize}
  $\Lambda{=}0$ shadow). Injected off-line pair $\delta_0{=}0.30\Rightarrow C{=}1.0023{>}1$ (detected); FORWARD\par
  flow \textbf{heals} it ($|\mathrm{Im}\,z|\,0.30\!\to\!0.269$, $C\to1.0014$). **Critical line = attractor of the\par
  flow, tracked by our detector** --- the rigorous form of the "stable attractor" instinct. *Guard-rail:* first\par
  seed used PSD $\sum vv^*$ (can't show $C>1$) \ensuremath{\to} fixed to the indefinite Weil quartet (matches B1); only then did\par
  detection+healing appear. \textbf{Honest caveat:} seed ran FORWARD (well-posed, healing trivial); the RH content is\par
  the BACKWARD/marginal direction (ill-posed), NOT tested. Lyapunov candidate refined to\par
  $\mathcal L=\sum(\mathrm{Im}\,z_j)^2$ (flow contracts it via partner-attraction $\dot z\ni-i/\mathrm{Im}\,z$).\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-25 headline.} Did NOT give up. Consolidated (P11) and opened a **genuinely new, non-self-referential\par
attack surface**: the de Bruijn--Newman heat flow ($\mathrm{RH}\iff\Lambda=0$), where reality is a theorem for\par

\subsection*{2026-06-04 --- Day 25 (cont.). GATE B resolved: clean Lyapunov theorem, but arithmetic-blind ? N5 dynamical no-go.}
\texttt{phase-8/\{GATE-B-verdict-sixth-language.md, experiments/gateB\_lyapunov.py\}}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Derived + verified the theorem:} under the Coulomb flow, $\mathcal L=\sum(\mathrm{Im}\,z_j)^2$ obeys
\end{itemize}
  $\dot{\mathcal L}=-2\sum_{j\ne k}(y_j-y_k)^2/|z_j-z_k|^2\le0$ (symmetrize $\dot{\mathcal L}=2\sum y_j\mathrm{Im}\dot z_j$).\par
  Matches finite-diff to machine precision. Clean, unconditional, NEW --- a strict Lyapunov function for the forward\par
  flow ($\Rightarrow$ "critical line is the attractor", now rigorous). By-product: isolated pair heals with\par
  $d(y^2)/dt=-2$ exactly $\Rightarrow$ any RH-violator sits at $|\mathrm{Im}|\le\sqrt{2\Lambda}\le0.63$.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{But it does NOT cross, for two verified reasons:} (1) \textbf{wrong direction} --- $\mathcal L$ decreases forward,
\end{itemize}
  so $\mathcal L(0)\ge\mathcal L(\Lambda)=0$ is trivial; (2) \textbf{arithmetic-blind} --- the identity is IDENTICAL for\par
  random / zeta-like / clustered configs; the ODE knows nothing about primes, so a pure-ODE Lyapunov would prove\par
  "every function satisfies RH" (false). RH lives in the INITIAL DATA; using it = re-injecting zeta's pair\par
  correlation = the \textbf{B1 wall}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{N5 (dynamical no-go, established):} any heat-flow/dissipative-dynamics RH attack using only the flow
\end{itemize}
  (Lyapunov from the ODE) cannot succeed --- arithmetic-blind. **Subsumes the forwarded PT-symmetry/neuromorphic\par
  suggestion** (any "critical-line-as-attractor" dissipative flow is of this type). The attractor picture is true\par
  and now rigorous, but not a proof, for a precise structural reason.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Honest continuation:} the productive version is Rodgers--Tao's (couple the flow to zeta's statistics; they got
\end{itemize}
  $\Lambda\ge0$ from the lower fluctuation control). RH $=\Lambda\le0$ needs the upper clustering control = open,\par
  RH-conditional pair correlation. Their machinery + B1 wall, $<2\%$.\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-25 cont. (Gate B).} Pushed the new path to its crux and got an honest, sharp result: a clean Lyapunov\par
THEOREM ($\dot{\mathcal L}\le0$) that rigorously vindicates the attractor intuition, plus a verified meta-theorem\par
(\textbf{N5}) that the entire flow-only class --- including the forwarded PT-symmetry ideas --- is arithmetic-blind and\par

\end{itemize}
  \textbf{positivity} ($\ge0$), oriented to give lower bounds / existence / the easy side; RH is fundamentally a one-sided\par

  This mismatch recurs across Gate B (monotonicity wrong way), N5/N6 (Weil $F\ge0$ = existence), T9-A (Montgomery\par

\end{itemize}
  $t_c/s^2<0$" --- a quantified target for the community.\par

\subsection*{2026-06-04 --- Day 27 (cont.). M10.2 --- the regularized Hodge gap SURVIVES (first non-trivially-realized positivity).}
\texttt{phase-10/\{M10.2-verdict-regularized-gap-survives.md, experiments/M10\_2\_regularized\_gap.py\}}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item The bare-gap vanishing (M10.1) was carried by TRIVIAL null directions (test functions vanishing at all window
\end{itemize}
  zeros = interpolation = the trivial classes). The curve Hodge index is definite on the PRIMITIVE part = modulo\par
  trivial. So the \textbf{regularized Hodge gap} = smallest POSITIVE eigenvalue of $\mathfrak t$ = $\lambda_{\min}$ of\par
  the $K\times K$ sine-kernel Gram of the zeros.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{MEASURED: it is POSITIVE and healthy} ($+0.15,0.34,0.48,0.69$ as $d$ resolves, at $T_0{=}100$; $+0.20,0.35$ at
\end{itemize}
  $T_0{=}500$) --- exactly where the bare gap vanished. **The genuine primitive intersection form of \ensuremath{\zeta} is\par
  positive-DEFINITE with a real gap** (the M10.1 degeneration was only trivial nullity). FIRST non-trivially-realized\par
  positivity in the program (every other language's relevant positivity was marginal).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Reformulation:} regularized Hodge index positivity $\iff G\succeq c>0$ uniformly $\iff$ zeros are a uniform
\end{itemize}
  \textbf{Riesz sequence} for Paley--Wiener/de Branges $\iff$ (U) as a \textbf{DETERMINANTAL positivity}. Still (U) (capped by\par
  the tightest pair), but now in the form $\zeta$-regularized determinants (Deninger $\det_\infty$, Connes--Consani)\par
  and Seip-type de Branges sampling are built for --- a TWO-sided definiteness, plausibly OUTSIDE the wrong-sign\par
  capstone (a determinant is positive or not, not a one-sided lower bound).\par
\begin{itemize}
\item Next M10.3: uniform lower frame bound --- does $\lambda_{\min}(G)$ stay bounded below as $T\to\infty$? (Seip de
\end{itemize}
  Branges sampling on the over-dense zero set.)\par

\begin{quote}\itshape
\textbf{Day-27 (cont.). M10.2: the first encouraging sign.} The regularized Hodge gap is positive and healthy --- the\par

\end{itemize}
  the foundation** --- it rests on real-stability of $\det(xI+\sum z_iA_i)$ for $A_i\succeq0$ (Borcea--Br?nd\\\'en), a\par

\end{itemize}
  hyperbolicity (stable polynomials) --- EVERY paradigm reduces to a positivity and to (U), including the one whose\par

  total positivity / real-stability of the PF sequence (modern language); the arithmetic-blindness (M11.3) + PSD\par
  foundation (M11.5) = the hyperbolicity-language forms of N5 and the capstone.\par

\subsection*{2026-06-05 --- Day 29. PHASE 12 executed in full (M12.1--M12.5, autonomous): the capstone is ESCAPED; N7 found and BRIDGED; lands on large values (Arc A).}

\end{itemize}
  $c=0.0465$ vs $1/(2\pi^2)=0.0507$ (8\%, confirmed). Tightest gaps ($\beta\approx0.18$--$0.25$) sit at the steepest\par
  $S$ rises ($dS/dT\approx1.3$).\par

  RH $\iff$ extreme normalized $S$-slope bounded uniformly.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{M12.4 --- the capstone test, DECISIVE:} the multiplicative-chaos UPPER bound is \$\textbackslash{}mathbb P(\textbackslash{}max S>u)\textbackslash{}le\textbackslash{}mathbb
\end{itemize}
  E[\textbackslash{}\#\textbackslash{}\{S>u\textbackslash{}\}]\$ (first moment / union bound / Markov) --- **NO PSD, NO SOS, NO real-stability. Genuinely NOT a\par
  positivity.\textbf{ }For the first time, the mechanism ESCAPES the wrong-sign capstone.**\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{M12.3 \textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}to\} N7 (the new, distinct wall):} the union-bound machinery is \textbf{probabilistic} (height-averaging =
\end{itemize}
  randomness); it controls the STATISTICS of the real zeros, not the DETERMINISTIC off-line count $N_{\rm off}$. So\par
  it \textbf{describes} the ensemble, does not \textbf{force} reality (B1 in probabilistic dress). The criterion that forces\par
  reality ($\lambda_{\min}(G)\ge0$ / $N_{\rm off}=0$) is again a positivity/deterministic-count = the capstone. **Two\par
  fundamental obstructions now named:** capstone (deterministic tools = positivities, wrong sign) + N7 (probabilistic\par

\end{itemize}
  $-\frac1\pi\sum\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n\log n}\sin(T\log n)$ (verified: tracks true $S(T)$, corr $0.79\to0.89$).\par
  So $\mathbb E[\#\{S>u\}]$ IS the deterministic prime-sum large-value count, bounded by the **LARGE SIEVE /\par
  Hal\\\'asz / moments --- deterministic + upper-direction + non-positivity: the FIRST tool that is all three** (the\par
  conjunction the capstone and N7 jointly demand). **Lands on the EXTREME large values of \ensuremath{\zeta} (resonance /\par

  exponents. \textbf{Rigorous core:} on squarefree $n$, $d_k(n)=k^{\omega(n)}$, so $d_k(n)^2=(k^2)^{\omega(n)}$; and\par
  $\sum_{n\le N}z^{\omega(n)}/n\sim(\log N)^z$ (Selberg--Delange). **So the moment exponent $k^2$ IS the per-prime\par
  \ensuremath{\omega}-weight $z=k^2$, factored $k\times k$** (one $k$ from $\zeta^k$, one from $\bar\zeta^k$). Explains P5 = moments =\par

  \textbf{large deviations of $\omega(n)$} (thick points = integers with $\omega(n)\sim z\log\log N$ prime factors,\par
  Sathe--Selberg). **Identifies the FHK/freezing frontier with the large-deviation theory of the number of prime\par
  factors** --- bridging modern extreme-value \ensuremath{\zeta}-theory to classical \ensuremath{\omega}(n) large deviations via Arc A.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}

\subsection*{2026-06-05 --- Day 32. STRATEGIC (advisor directive): where the \ensuremath{\omega}-structure touches the zeros --- the explicit formula is \ensuremath{\omega}-BLIND; the exact bridge is Motohashi / the spectral theory of moments.}
\texttt{phase-14/STRATEGIC-where-omega-touches-the-zeros.md}.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item The advisor's directive supersedes the others: don't refine FHK; find where the \ensuremath{\omega}-structure touches the zeros
\end{itemize}
  EXACTLY (a sum over zeros / explicit formula), not a statistic of values.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{NEGATIVE half (structural obstruction):} $\omega(p^a)=1$ on ALL prime powers = the support of $\Lambda$. So
\end{itemize}
  $\Lambda(n)z^{\omega(n)}=z\Lambda(n)$: \textbf{the explicit formula (the canonical sum over zeros) is \textbackslash{}ensuremath\{\textbackslash{}omega\}-BLIND} --- the\par
  \ensuremath{\omega}-weight is a trivial factor $z$. The \ensuremath{\omega}-large-deviations (many-factor integers) are ORTHOGONAL to the\par
  prime-power support of the explicit formula. This is the precise reason Phase-13 (maxima/moments/freezing) does\par
  not move RH: it is a statistic of values, invisible to the explicit formula.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{The leading moment factorizes} $a_k g_k(\log T)^{k^2}$: \ensuremath{\omega} gives $a_k$, zeros give $g_k$, DECOUPLED (product).
\end{itemize}
  So neither the explicit formula nor the leading moment couples \ensuremath{\omega} to the zeros.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{POSITIVE half (the exact bridge):} the coupling is the OFF-DIAGONAL = the shifted-convolution / additive-divisor
\end{itemize}
  problem, which touches the zeros EXACTLY via the \textbf{spectral theory of moments}: \textbf{Motohashi's formula} ($k=2$,\par
  the 4th moment = exact spectral sum over the Maass-form spectrum + the zeros), PROVEN; CFKRS / $GL(k)$ for $k\ge3$,\par
  conjectural. THIS is the first exact point where the \ensuremath{\omega}/divisor structure meets the zeros --- an identity, not a\par
  statistic.\par
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{RH-directed redirection:} study the off-diagonal of the $d_k$ moments and its spectral (Motohashi/$GL(k)$)
\end{itemize}
  expansion, where the zeros appear exactly; ask whether the \ensuremath{\omega}-large-deviation structure constrains the spectral/zero\par
  side. Honest caveats: brings in the automorphic spectrum (deep machinery); $k\ge3$ open (the moment wall, spectral\par
  form); whether it gives NEW zero-info is open --- but it is the right KIND of object. Filter (per advisor): if a step\par
  factors through $\Lambda$/prime powers, \ensuremath{\omega} is trivial there = wrong step. Next: M14.1 (additive divisor \ensuremath{\leftrightarrow} zeros via\par
  Motohashi, explicitly).\par

\begin{quote}\itshape

\end{itemize}
  cuspidal structure; at cuspidal points it multiplies the Maass contribution by zeta(1/2+i kappa\_j)\textasciicircum{}\{2(z-1)\} ---\par

\end{itemize}

\subsection*{2026-06-05 --- Day 33. N8 --- the density\ensuremath{\to}absence gap characterized: the square-root cancellation barrier (= the capstone).}

  the aggregate is power-saving-but-growing \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} one zero below resolution \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} density not absence.\par

\end{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  describe not force) = meta-obstruction (no deterministic non-positivity absence) = N8 (power-saving ? square-root).\par
  Square-root cancellation = upper-cancellation = the capstone's upper constraint = RH. One object: the absence of\par

\end{itemize}
  clever tool-combination could supply; the central barrier itself. No further STATISTIC helps; the exact lines are\par

\subsection*{2026-06-04 --- Day 35. The ANCHOR FRAMEWORK: anchor = Landau singularity (\ensuremath{\zeta}-free). A classification of zero-absence mechanisms.}

\end{itemize}
  (non-negative-coefficient) measure (Landau 1905). No \ensuremath{\zeta}, no "pole," no HP/Weil/RH in the definition. The pole of \ensuremath{\zeta} at\par
  s=1 is merely the INSTANCE for the prime measure. The audit's test is passed \ensuremath{\to} a genuine object.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  \ensuremath{\Sigma}w\_j Re K(s\_j,\ensuremath{\cdot})\ensuremath{\ge}0 on supp \ensuremath{\nu}); anchor (s\_* where the transform =+\ensuremath{\infty} = Landau singularity, REAL by Landau); tight vs\par
  loose budget (tight=pinned by anchor\ensuremath{\Rightarrow}absence; loose=estimated\ensuremath{\Rightarrow}density).\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  EXACTLY to de la Vall\\\'ee Poussin (\ensuremath{\nu}=prime measure, K=e\textasciicircum{}\{-su\}, s\_*=1, sum rule 3+4cos\ensuremath{\theta}+cos2\ensuremath{\theta}, budget B=convexity log t,\par
  reach \ensuremath{\delta}\ensuremath{\asymp}1/log t). The classical theorem IS the s\_*=1 instance. No conjecture.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  (\ensuremath{\sigma}=1/2 via self-adjoint spectral measure, real axis), Weil (\ensuremath{\sigma}=1/2 via functional eq), P7\ensuremath{\to}T4 (\ensuremath{\sigma}=1/2 variational),\par
  function-field RH (diagonal, Hodge index --- PROVEN geometric anchor). All = manufacture a Landau-type anchor, differing\par

\end{itemize}
  prime measure's only forced singularity at \ensuremath{\sigma}=1, NOT \ensuremath{\sigma}=1/2 --- so no anchor at the center \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} density. N8's square-root\par

\end{itemize}
  density. Evidence: ALL known analytic zero-free regions are positivity+pole; the only proven RH (function field) is\par
  positivity+Hodge-anchor. No known counterexample. NOT claimed proven.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  problem, not cancellation --- different from N8, NOT collapsed. Subsumes HP + Weil as two proposals for the same object.\par

  What IS established: the \ensuremath{\zeta}-free DEFINITION (Landau), Theorem A (de la Vall\\\'ee Poussin recovered), and RH reframed as a\par

\end{itemize}

\subsection*{2026-06-04 --- Day 36. STAGES 1 \& 2: the Landau anchor tested against the one PROVEN RH. Verdict: it COLLAPSES, informatively.}
\texttt{phase-14/STAGE1-2-anchor-vs-definiteness-the-verdict.md}. The audit ran both stages to settle the bifurcation: is the\par
anchor a NEW object or a renaming? The named danger --- the function-field anchor is "just the trivial cohomology class" ---\par
MATERIALIZED.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  \ensuremath{\sigma}\_a (Landau), convexity budget B(t), non-neg cosine poly P \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} no zero with \ensuremath{\beta}>\ensuremath{\sigma}\_a?c(P,\ensuremath{\rho})/B(\ensuremath{\gamma}). NO "\ensuremath{\zeta}" in the statement\par
  \ensuremath{\Rightarrow} the anchor has independent existence (test passed). BUT it is recognizably the CLASSICAL positive-coefficient\par

  it never reaches the center (no arithmetic positive measure has abscissa = critical line).\par

  (H?) = RH. So anchors are at the EDGE (s=0,1), NO anchor at s=1/2 --- exactly like \ensuremath{\zeta}. RH proven by the HODGE INDEX THEOREM\par
  on S=C\ensuremath{\times}C (intersection form signature (1,\ensuremath{\rho}?1), negative-definite on \ensuremath{\langle}f?,f?\ensuremath{\rangle}\textasciicircum{}\ensuremath{\perp}), forcing |\ensuremath{\alpha}\_i|=\ensuremath{\sqrt{}}q. The fiber classes\par
  f?,f? (ample anchors) = H?,H\ensuremath{^2} = the edge poles. THE CENTER IS REACHED BY DEFINITENESS (signature), NOT BY AN ANCHOR.\par

\end{itemize}
  measure transform, lives at the EDGE, present for \ensuremath{\zeta} (pole at s=1). DEFINITENESS = signature of a form/operator (Hodge\par
  index / Weil positivity / self-adjointness), acts at the CENTER, gives RH, ABSENT for \ensuremath{\zeta} (the capstone). My earlier ?3\par
  table wrongly listed HP/Weil/Hodge as "anchors at \ensuremath{\sigma}=1/2" --- they are DEFINITENESS, not anchors. Stage 2 separates them.\par

\end{itemize}
  NOT the discriminator. RH-where-proven uses the Hodge index theorem = Weil positivity = the capstone. The danger\par
  ("anchor = trivial cohomology class") was real and confirmed.\par
\begin{itemize}

\end{itemize}
  ON A 2-DIMENSIONAL ARITHMETIC GEOMETRY over Spec(\ensuremath{\mathbb{Z}}) --- an object playing the role of C\ensuremath{\times}C\par

\subsection*{2026-06-05 --- Day 40. Three non-circular tracks advanced in parallel (Options 1, 2, 4).}
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{OPT 1 (\texttt{OPT1-c-reduction-selberg-tail.md}):} exact split V=N\ensuremath{\int}\_\{|\ensuremath{\alpha}|<1\}+N\ensuremath{\int}\_\{1\ensuremath{\le}|\ensuremath{\alpha}|\ensuremath{\le}A\} ?? F. Low part (I) \ensuremath{\ll} N

  UNCONDITIONAL (diagonal L\ensuremath{\cdot}T\textasciicircum{}\{-2|\ensuremath{\alpha}|\} + F\ensuremath{\ge}0; no loss). The ENTIRE loss is the high part (II) = uniform \ensuremath{\int}\_1\textasciicircum{}A F(\ensuremath{\alpha})d\ensuremath{\alpha}.\par

  Goldston--Montgomery short-interval variance. Sub-RH, non-circular; each smoothing improvement = measurable\par
  decrement of c.\par
